The downsides with this though, it will hurt to be without them. But suddenly, asynchronous Javascrip is fun!
Not to mention, that Observables are lazy, compared to the eager nature of Promises. Going into Observables at start may hurt (your head) a bit, but it's very worth the effort.
In general, if you're not going full-on imperative with your programming, Observables are worth your time. They're like Promises done right, and then some more.

Don't start with RxJS though. Use Kefir instead. RxJS is so outlandisly MS'y in its documentation. #es7 #javascript
Here we see a react engineer deploying a contact form 
@Sohaib_Nehal Not really, if we're thinking of those things as data structures, while async/await does an implicit Promise resolve/reject-throw under the hood. Which I think is good for imperative-style stuff, try-catching rejected Promises there and then.
@vivainio @VesaKarvonen In an imperative environment most likely yeah, if thinking of data as pure Javascript values. Passing boxed values (Promises, Observables) around is cleaner, but the advantages are partly lost because of the eager nature of Promises.

There's also a sense of magic with composing optics, because you're not necessarily used to things "just working".
There's an entirely new and exciting world with using lenses, where when you first get the gist of them, they turn out to be very powerful.
Two months into this React project, and zero `this`, `new` or `class` keywords in the codebase. Lovely!
State in this case is just a lensed view into some data that will be passed on.
Thus, any field will behave in a predictable manner since its output isâ€”sans keyboard inputâ€”solely dependent on the state you give it.
This also allows for creating grouped optics where you're passing the value _and_ validation to your form fields.
The result, combined with L.pick, is a structure of all invalid data. Then, form-level validation is just `result.map(R.isEmpty)`.
Form validation through lenses is brilliantly simple: specify your validation through L.when and similar operations.
